    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_159632072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159632072" />
    <a title="Carole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1572466-carole"><img alt="Carole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1235218515p2/1572466.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159632072?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carole" href="/user/show/1572466-carole">Carole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906040345" href="/book/show/9894790-where-would-i-be-without-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1572466-carole?shelf=san-fransisco">san-fransisco</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1572466-carole?shelf=guillaume-musso">guillaume-musso</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1572466-carole?shelf=paris">paris</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159632072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4632488127106748873">I really wanted to enjoy this book, it had all the ingredients of a fascinating story, the enigmatic cover of a woman alone on a beach, an unrequited love, a cop looking for a world famous art thief, set in France and the USA, obsessive characters …........ but in the end I just felt quite disappointed.<br/><br/>I thought the main storyline was too coincidental, it just didn’t feel plausible to me. If I said what it was it would be a huge spoiler. <br/><br/>I didn’t really empathise with the main characters either,</span>
  <span id="freeText4632488127106748873" style="display:none">I really wanted to enjoy this book, it had all the ingredients of a fascinating story, the enigmatic cover of a woman alone on a beach, an unrequited love, a cop looking for a world famous art thief, set in France and the USA, obsessive characters …........ but in the end I just felt quite disappointed.<br /><br />I thought the main storyline was too coincidental, it just didn’t feel plausible to me. If I said what it was it would be a huge spoiler. <br /><br />I didn’t really empathise with the main characters either, Gabrielle, Martin and Archibald. I didn’t feel that I really knew them any more by the end than I did at the beginning. They didn’t seem to know what they thought and kept changing their minds so I didn’t know their inner mind workings, and therefore I found myself not caring too much about what happened to them.<br /><br />I also wondered whether there was such a thing as product placement in a book? I lost count of the number of times a particular brand of fizzy drink was drunk, or a certain mp3 player was used, I actually found that quite annoying by the end.<br /><br />I did think it was well translated though, if i didn’t know it was originally written in French, I wouldn’t have known, the writing flowed very easily and the dialogue seemed natural.<br /><br />So, even though it was not my type of book I’m sure that some people would enjoy it, after all the cover reads that ‘over 1 million copies sold worldwide’!<br /><br />From <a href="http://carolesbooks.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Carole's Book Corner</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4632488127106748873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2126388672" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2126388672" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30833806-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583342625p2/30833806.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2126388672?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/30833806-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906040345" href="/book/show/9894790-where-would-i-be-without-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2126388672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17990000097515307312"> So if you've read some of my other reviews you will know I'm fairly big on recommendations for books by other people. I'm always open to trying new authors when people tell me about them. Which is how I came to find out about Musso. There was only one slight problem here. This author doesn't have to many books translated in to English. And my friend who isn't English had read a bunch of his books that where much more in the crime genre and haven't been translated yet. But I figured she loved hi</span>
  <span id="freeText17990000097515307312" style="display:none"> So if you've read some of my other reviews you will know I'm fairly big on recommendations for books by other people. I'm always open to trying new authors when people tell me about them. Which is how I came to find out about Musso. There was only one slight problem here. This author doesn't have to many books translated in to English. And my friend who isn't English had read a bunch of his books that where much more in the crime genre and haven't been translated yet. But I figured she loved his work so much that what the heck I'd pick it up and give it a go. <br /><br /> Musso's ability to create enticing character is one you have to give him credit for. The star crossed lovers is one that's been written about since Shakespeare. Martin and Gabrielle starts out as teenagers in love but for reason unknown to Martin things don't work out the way he hopes. There love is like that of all people their age. It burns hot and fast and then is gone. Martin is the epitome of the tortured soul for ever carrying a flame for his lost love. Whilst Gabrielle seem to be trying to put right what once went wrong. Throwing in Archibald is like the chaos element of the story. The characters come of well and are whole enough to give the story meaning. <br /><br /> The authors writing is quick and light. He manages to create this world that harks back to films of the sixties. The intrepid cop on the hunt for and elusive art thief comes out like some mix of James bond and the Thomas crown affair. I like his style very much and he manages to present us with this magical world. Now this is not one for the die hard crime fans. The romance plays out in the for front of everything that happens through out the story. And while some time is spent on the crimes of Archibald this is not what is most on the authors mind. I feel this book could only really have been written by a French author or possible one from south America. The prose are slightly over the top and whimsical. Also at times the story stretches in to fantasy. But in this case it fits the story. And who doesn't like a bit of escapism. He speak about love as this mythical creature which I don't think really exist in the real world. it does however makes for and entertaining story.<br /><br /> This book come from a genre I don't normal look to pick up. I'm much more in to the dark and dirty side of crime. But in this case it was a nice detour from my usual fair. It doesn't take to long to make your way through the pages. And I found my self having to smile when it got to the end . He is an author I would be inclined to return to in the future. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17990000097515307312" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_152639087" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152639087" />
    <a title="Marleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/348805-marleen"><img alt="Marleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1225138538p2/348805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152639087?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marleen" href="/user/show/348805-marleen">Marleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906040345" href="/book/show/9894790-where-would-i-be-without-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152639087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1459621433338489772">The copy of this book I read was an uncorrected bound proof, kindly send to me for my opinion by Bookhugger through the RealReaders programme. The book is due to be published here on April 4th, 2011.<br/><br/>This is the story about Martin Beaumont, a young man from Paris, France who while spending a summer in San Francisco where he meets Gabrielle with whom he falls deeply and irrevocably in love. But once the summer is over he returns to France and it seems that their chance at love has been lost foreve</span>
  <span id="freeText1459621433338489772" style="display:none">The copy of this book I read was an uncorrected bound proof, kindly send to me for my opinion by Bookhugger through the RealReaders programme. The book is due to be published here on April 4th, 2011.<br /><br />This is the story about Martin Beaumont, a young man from Paris, France who while spending a summer in San Francisco where he meets Gabrielle with whom he falls deeply and irrevocably in love. But once the summer is over he returns to France and it seems that their chance at love has been lost forever for reasons Martin doesn't know or understand.<br />Years later Martin is a successful but bitter detective in Paris on the hunt of notorious art thief, Archibald Maclean, a hunt that turns into an obsession.<br />But is Martin really chasing Maclean or is Maclean playing a game with Martin?<br />When Maclean travels to San Francisco preparing for his nex big theft, Martin follows him there. And in San Francisco Martin will face Maclean as well as a love he thought lost forever and big questions about life and death.<br />What to say about this book. It is completely unlike anything I've read before, and it wasn't at all what I expected from the blurb. I was expecting a thriller in which a cop follows a master criminal combined with a love story. And those aspects where certainly in the book. But, it was much more than that and even the term magical realism doesn't seem adequate when I'm trying to classify this novel. The book was too philosphical to be simply filed under thriller and too dark to be qualified as a simple love story. The last quarter of the book plays out in an otherworldly realm which stretches the reader's ability to suspend disbelieve to its outer limits, and for some probably beyond those limits.<br />In some aspects this story was a bit too simple for me, all the links a bit too convenient and explanations to easily accepted by all involved. In other parts though, the story took me to completely unexpected places which, while fascinating, also seemed a bit too far-fetched.<br />Having said all that, the book captured me almost from the first page, and although I did find the ending a bit contrived and convenient, it did put a happy smile on my face. And that is the reason I mark this book 4-, despite my reservations as far as some parts of the story are concerned.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1459621433338489772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906040345" href="/book/show/9894790-where-would-i-be-without-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2076629830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15072266778560229680">Coincidentally beautiful despite the chick flick style, easy to read and annoying at times. Just the book I needed to make a break with between serious books.<br/><br/>If you are in need of a simple yet sophisticated novel which is all about love, betrayal, disappointment and yet more love with a happy ending then this is it. You will undoubtedly love and hate all the main characters with the fierce impression of being betrayed by Archibald playing God with so many lives. Only to resurface all over again </span>
  <span id="freeText15072266778560229680" style="display:none">Coincidentally beautiful despite the chick flick style, easy to read and annoying at times. Just the book I needed to make a break with between serious books.<br /><br />If you are in need of a simple yet sophisticated novel which is all about love, betrayal, disappointment and yet more love with a happy ending then this is it. You will undoubtedly love and hate all the main characters with the fierce impression of being betrayed by Archibald playing God with so many lives. Only to resurface all over again and relove him for his struggle to fix his mistakes. <br /><br />Unusual events happen in this book, so many that it left me dumbfounded by the sheer belief that love can be so strong as to cross the boundaries between life and death, coincidence and prudence. It is, all in all, a beautiful strong love story, with wild souls looking for redemptions and a balance between past and future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15072266778560229680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_172783137" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172783137" />
    <a title="Shaz Goodwin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4422203-shaz-goodwin"><img alt="Shaz Goodwin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605022219p2/4422203.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172783137?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shaz Goodwin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shaz Goodwin" href="/user/show/4422203-shaz-goodwin">Shaz Goodwin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906040345" href="/book/show/9894790-where-would-i-be-without-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172783137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5760670276584427626">In this story of second chances we have three genres to hold our attention – romance, crime and the supernatural.<br/><br/>At the start of the journey each of the characters are finding their way while carrying their unhealed emotional wounds. These wounds distort their interaction with the world of emotion. We follow the characters as they confront their fears and weaknesses through crises to become whole. <br/><br/>Gabrielle, Martin and Archibald are linked but only Archibald knows how. <br/><br/>The story is set in San Fr</span>
  <span id="freeText5760670276584427626" style="display:none">In this story of second chances we have three genres to hold our attention – romance, crime and the supernatural.<br /><br />At the start of the journey each of the characters are finding their way while carrying their unhealed emotional wounds. These wounds distort their interaction with the world of emotion. We follow the characters as they confront their fears and weaknesses through crises to become whole. <br /><br />Gabrielle, Martin and Archibald are linked but only Archibald knows how. <br /><br />The story is set in San Francisco and Paris. Gabrielle lives in San Francisco and is studying at Berkeley. Martin lives in Paris and has gone to San Francisco to improve his English and explore. They meet on campus in the Berkeley cafeteria where Martin is working to make ends meet. Their time together during the summer is innocent until the day Martin is due to depart. Gabrielle receives a letter in which Martin tells her of his feelings. She makes it to the airport on time, Martin is able to take another ten days away and so follows their ten days of intimacy and love. Their relationship doesn’t make the long distance. <br /><br />The two settings are beautifully described with just enough information and focus that I was able to imagine myself in these two cities without ever having visited them.<br /><br />Martin qualifies to join the police and we then get to meet Archibald as Martin becomes more and more obsessed with capturing him. Archibald is an art thief who has been elusive for many years. It’s during this part of the story that we realise Archibald has been able to manipulate events, even from a distance.<br /><br />There were a couple of twists that I hadn’t anticipated which made me stop and think (mainly because I was confused). I had to re-evaluate what I already knew. I love stories that have this effect on me. Anything that takes me out of the normal confines of my mind can only be a good thing! <br /><br />When we hit (what I honestly thought was) the final crisis point, I wondered where the story could possibly lead to next ………………. I wasn’t prepared for where the story took me. Nothing I’d read before had made me think that I would be reading about the paranormal/supernatural. It took me a while to adjust to this change but once I did, I thought it was actually a very imaginative way for resolution …………….. I don’t think it would have been the same in any other way! <br /><br />The characters are in depth and the plot/sub-plots are brilliant. The story will hold your attention throughout. If you’ve been reading any of my review blogs you will know that makes a story a big hit with me.<br /><br />The quotations at the start of each new section are so apt for what you are about to read. Lovely to get that ‘extra’ touch in the format of a novel.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5760670276584427626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_213020531" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/213020531" />
    <a title="Yla Socorro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6401363-yla-socorro"><img alt="Yla Socorro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566311752p2/6401363.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/213020531?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yla Socorro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yla Socorro" href="/user/show/6401363-yla-socorro">Yla Socorro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906040345" href="/book/show/9894790-where-would-i-be-without-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer213020531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18321972290316641577">Introduction: I trusted to read this book partially because I loved the first book I read by Guillaume Musso (Will You Be There). But to tell you honestly, the beginning part was fab. But the ending... well the least I can say is that, "it just didn't impress me much!" :p<br/><br/>Overview: Parisian cop Martin Beaumont has never really got over his first love, Gabrielle. Their brief, intense affair in San Francisco and the pain of her rejection still haunt him years later.<br/>Now, however, he’s a successful d</span>
  <span id="freeText18321972290316641577" style="display:none">Introduction: I trusted to read this book partially because I loved the first book I read by Guillaume Musso (Will You Be There). But to tell you honestly, the beginning part was fab. But the ending... well the least I can say is that, "it just didn't impress me much!" :p<br /><br />Overview: Parisian cop Martin Beaumont has never really got over his first love, Gabrielle. Their brief, intense affair in San Francisco and the pain of her rejection still haunt him years later.<br />Now, however, he’s a successful detective – and tonight he’s going to arrest the legendary art thief, Archibald Maclean, when he raids the Musée d’Orsay for a priceless Van Gogh.<br />But the enigmatic Archibald has other plans.<br />Martin’s pursuit of the master criminal across Paris is the first step in an adventure that will take him back to San Francisco, and to the edge of love and life itself.<br /><br />My opinion: This is a really ‘different’ read, with no clear genre to categorize it with. It’s a love story, a police thriller and then turns towards the paranormal at the end. So a bit of everything, really.<br />Set in Paris and San Francisco in the mid 90s, the story revolves around Gabrielle and Martin – a young couple who met during their younger days and fell in love. The story leaps forward to find Martin working as a French policeman with a special interest in art crime. Martin and Gabrielle have not met since that summer twelve years before and it is clear that both their lives has gone pretty empty and lonely.<br />Martin is determined to capture the famous art thief Archibald Maclean who has outsmarted him for many years. His chase led him back to San Francisco.<br /><br />It’s an interesting read, a unique plot line and although I had guessed a couple of the twists, it’s an entertaining read.<br /><br />The story enters into the paranormal at the close, which was for me, a safe way of explaining some things and tied the story up quite well, but on a personal level I really didn't like. Anyway, I still enjoyed reading this book. Its different, and some of you might just like it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18321972290316641577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText3398623260513497178" style="display:none">This was my first time reading a book from this author and I am totally thankful to my bestfriend who decided to give it to me! It really was different from the books I usually enjoy reading, but thankfully, it caught my attention! I liked the development of the plot and the innovative writing style of the author. I liked the alternation of plans and how we discovered each characer individually nd he really did built his characters very well! <br>Throughout the book I couldn't help but stop and contemplate some very well put words that will really remain with me for a long time.<br><br>“It's scary being loved. Because life is complicated and all too often it throws you off balance by sending you the right person at the wrong time.”<br><br>I loved this very much! I also liked the idea that sometimes love is most intense when it isn't consumed. That idea really threw me off.<br><br>Also, as a fan of actually imagining how the characters look like and creating an image about them, I just tried to find someone perfect enough to be Martin and Gabrielle. However, the only two persons who came in my mind and who I'll be sticking with whenever I will think of this book are Will and Riley from Sense8. Aren't they perfect for the roles? Even though the descriptions may ot fit perfectly.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455368505i/18093551._SX540_.jpg" width="640" height="292" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455368505i/18093552.jpg" width="308" height="207" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Really lovely book! ♥<br></span>

<div id="review_1192043894" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1192043894" />
    <a title="Helen Albert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2028488-helen-albert"><img alt="Helen Albert" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1192043894?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen Albert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen Albert" href="/user/show/2028488-helen-albert">Helen Albert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1192043894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1228985967030100341">Where would I be without you (English translation from original French) tells the story of a French policeman Martin Beaumont, his early and continued love for an American girl called Gabrielle and the story of his obsession with and pursuit of a great art thief called Archibald Maclean.<br/><br/>I have read several other book in this sort of style and genre, which I greatly enjoyed, for example the James Twining novels, but this novel really grated with me. I think it may have partly been the way it was </span>
  <span id="freeText1228985967030100341" style="display:none">Where would I be without you (English translation from original French) tells the story of a French policeman Martin Beaumont, his early and continued love for an American girl called Gabrielle and the story of his obsession with and pursuit of a great art thief called Archibald Maclean.<br /><br />I have read several other book in this sort of style and genre, which I greatly enjoyed, for example the James Twining novels, but this novel really grated with me. I think it may have partly been the way it was translated. I have read quite a few books in translation and in my experience the skill of the translator makes a huge difference to how well the book reads in English. <br /><br />However, in addition to this there were several bits of the story that seemed pretty implausible. For example, the somewhat fantastical ending and Martin suddenly dropping everything and going to America in search of Archibald and being given the right to arrest him on US soil. I’m also not sure how well the love story/crime combination worked in this case. It can be done well, but this seemed more like a love story than a crime novel.<br /><br />It is a shame, as the general premise for the story is not bad (although very similar to several other books), but unfortunately it fails to deliver on many counts.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1228985967030100341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3156118904" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906040345" href="/book/show/9894790-where-would-i-be-without-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9701638-krissy?shelf=new-reads-2020">new-reads-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3156118904&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3156118904" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1337836259402375158">This book was easy to read and not entirely predictable. I made the mistake of finishing it late at night so I don’t feel like saying a whole lot about it, but here are some Quick Thoughts:<br/><br/>- Coke and Coke Zero are mentioned too many times for me not to question whether this book was financially backed in some way by the Coca Cola Company. <br/><br/>- I liked the contrast between the experience of age and the impetuosity of youth. <br/><br/>- The ending got Very Weird, folks. The last 50 pages took like a star and a</span>
  <span id="freeText1337836259402375158" style="display:none">This book was easy to read and not entirely predictable. I made the mistake of finishing it late at night so I don’t feel like saying a whole lot about it, but here are some Quick Thoughts:<br /><br />- Coke and Coke Zero are mentioned too many times for me not to question whether this book was financially backed in some way by the Coca Cola Company. <br /><br />- I liked the contrast between the experience of age and the impetuosity of youth. <br /><br />- The ending got Very Weird, folks. The last 50 pages took like a star and a half off my rating of this book. <br /><br />- Quote I liked: “Fearing the worst was far more frightening than knowing the worst.”<br /><br />- Quote that made me roll my eyes: “The expression got under his skin like a snake bite, putting ice crystals in his veins and fracturing the wall of stone around his heart.” Such DRAMA?!?!? And also just way too many separate images going on there, friend. <br /><br />- Quote(s) I hated: Any and all quotes that made stereotyping generalizations about male and female behavior or compared females to precious stones (this here is where we get the word “objectify”). <br /><br />- Quote I REALLY hated: “Never stopping to admit to herself what she knew really: that she needed a compass to guide her, arms to embrace her and fists to protect her.“ YIKES. <br /><br />Implicit sexism notwithstanding, there was a lot said about Gabrielle’s baggage and Problems™️, but we didn’t get to see it go down, and we CERTAINLY never get it from her point of view. Hands-down she is the most important and yet most underdeveloped character in this book — we never get to understand her motivations, beyond being told by the male characters that she’s let herself be used and abused by all the men in her life. The real abuse here, I think, is giving a character agency to kind of f*ck over the male hero and then ending the book before she gets a platform to speak for herself. <br /><br />I said a lot more than I meant to, but I could say a lot more still. Anyone else wish Gabrielle were better developed? <br /><br />Two stars because I really wouldn’t recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1337836259402375158" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10341209521024794716" style="display:none">I have really mixed feelings about this book. As much as I love Guillaume Musso's writing, this time it annoyed me terribly. <div id="review_2596194253" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2596194253" />
    <a title="Katerina Shipilova" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51427985-katerina-shipilova"><img alt="Katerina Shipilova" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452584335p2/51427985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2596194253?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina Shipilova" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina Shipilova" href="/user/show/51427985-katerina-shipilova">Katerina Shipilova</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2596194253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2248492568407489961">I read this book to expand my French vocabulary, and it was just great for that. Easy to read and lots of useful phrases. Apart from that, I would say it's a rather strange book. People talk to each other with cliché phrases, which feel completely unrealistic. Some random stories about a lost prostitute or a depressive teenager come up, which don't really contribute to the story line. Relaxed reading, but a bit annoying sometimes.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_144185807" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144185807" />
    <a title="CuteBadger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4084869-cutebadger"><img alt="CuteBadger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286982399p2/4084869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144185807?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CuteBadger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CuteBadger" href="/user/show/4084869-cutebadger">CuteBadger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906040345" href="/book/show/9894790-where-would-i-be-without-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144185807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13787106041516527189">A young Frenchman has a life-changing love affair while in America. Some years later he has become a policeman in the Paris Art Squad and has a cat-and-mouse relationship with a serial art thief.<br/><br/>According to the cover, more than 1 million copies of this book have already been sold worldwide. That surprises me a great deal as, to my mind, there’s a lot wrong with it and several aspects of it feel forced and clunky.<br/><br/>The most obvious problem appears to be with the translation, which seems very liter</span>
  <span id="freeText13787106041516527189" style="display:none">A young Frenchman has a life-changing love affair while in America. Some years later he has become a policeman in the Paris Art Squad and has a cat-and-mouse relationship with a serial art thief.<br /><br />According to the cover, more than 1 million copies of this book have already been sold worldwide. That surprises me a great deal as, to my mind, there’s a lot wrong with it and several aspects of it feel forced and clunky.<br /><br />The most obvious problem appears to be with the translation, which seems very literal (i.e. translating the strict meaning of the words rather than the general sense). As someone who has fluent French and has done her fair share of translation, I found the novel poorly translated, the language simplistic and frankly irritating. The poor translation effectively put up a barrier between myself and the story, meaning that I couldn’t get swept up in it. Some of the references to French culture should perhaps have also been removed and substituted for something more universal, as non-Gallic readers will largely not get the benefit of them. <br /><br />The book doesn’t seem to know what it wants to be or even what form it wants to take. It’s a strange mix of chick-lit, thriller and at least one other genre (trying to avoid spoilers here!). The text sometimes appears in the usual way for a novel and at other times the reader is faced with essentially a film script, with the names of the characters followed by their dialogue.<br /><br />Musso also repeatedly uses some tricks in his writing in order to give a sense of the various times in which the action takes place. His favourite, which he uses over and over again, is to have popular songs playing or other cultural phenomena discussed so that his narrator can comment on how successful a particular band were in a certain year for example. This trick is used over and over again, so becomes quite grating and intrusive – it gets particularly bad in a passage where the book’s protagonist goes to the supermarket to buy some essentials and tells us that in his basket he has food, the latest novel by a world-famous thriller writer and a DVD box set of a cult TV series. He also demonstrates an obsession with a particular fizzy drink to the extent that the reader suspects product placement, and has pretty much every character at some stage wear a leather jacket.<br /><br />The novel’s characters aren’t any more original and are clichéd in the extreme. One in particular is described as looking like a certain Hollywood actor and Musso then uses that actor’s biographical details for his character. There are other “borrowings” (or perhaps homages) to classic detective fiction in the naming of one of the minor characters.<br /><br />But, having said all that, it’s a quick read and something keeps you pressing on right to the (not-wholly-successful) end. Indeed, near the end I even found a couple of passages quite moving. <br /><br />All in all, very French, very clichéd, but very undemanding, so will be the perfect holiday read for many. Readers looking for something more realistic or demanding would do well to steer clear.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13787106041516527189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_142203405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/142203405" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/546484-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500388520p2/546484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/142203405?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/546484-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906040345" href="/book/show/9894790-where-would-i-be-without-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer142203405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13803881424411435332">Guillaume Musso is a young French author who is very successful in his home land. He has sold over 8 million books and Where Would I Be Without You? has already sold over a million in France. The version published in the UK is translated by Anna Brown and Anna Aitken and will be released on 4 April 2011.<br/><br/>This is a really 'different' read, with no clear genre category to put it into. It's a love story, a police thriller and then turns towards the paranormal towards the end, so a bit of everything </span>
  <span id="freeText13803881424411435332" style="display:none">Guillaume Musso is a young French author who is very successful in his home land. He has sold over 8 million books and Where Would I Be Without You? has already sold over a million in France. The version published in the UK is translated by Anna Brown and Anna Aitken and will be released on 4 April 2011.<br /><br />This is a really 'different' read, with no clear genre category to put it into. It's a love story, a police thriller and then turns towards the paranormal towards the end, so a bit of everything really. This works well if like me, you have a fairly eclectic reading taste, however die-hard crime fans may not enjoy the different directions that the story takes.<br /><br />Set in Paris and San Franscisco in the mid 90s, the story centres around Gabrielle and Martin - a young couple who meet and fall in love. The story leaps forward to find Martin working as a 'flic' - a French policeman with a special interest in art crime. Martin and Gabrielle have not met since that summer twelve years before and it is clear that Martin's life is pretty empty and lonely. <br /><br />Martin is determined to capture the famous art thief Archibald Maclean who has outsmarted him for many years and goes back to America to chase him. <br /><br />Gabrielle, Archibald and Martin are linked together in ways that only Archibald knows, he has been instrumental in their lives for a long time and from a distance.<br /><br />I don't want to give away any spoilers in this review so won't go into the storyline any further. It's an interesting read, a unique plot line and although I had guessed a couple of the twists, it's an entertaining read.<br /><br />The style of writing changes throughout the book, with parts reading like a screenplay and others like a diary - sometimes the language can be too simple and a little stilted, this may be due to the translation rather than the author's intention.<br /><br />The story enters into the paranormal at the close, which was a neat way of explaining some things and tied the story up quite well, but on a personal level didn't really work for me.<br /><br />On the whole an easy, entertaining read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13803881424411435332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2o+BeODRxkqFw9MMz/we/bFKnR3TsT+QCwvW5BePliQimDh1o3Xpmd8UIViGEivpHmEbuQ5vKCSxkGG5hUYoyg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FGLZvF6JTER4YJFBFwas3Xn643VK9Toab1tLaKp1m3jsdWCxHS1jlyK3YxVe6JnJ1tFl0ZcrLa7VwPw1OLwllg==')})
  }

Years earlier they had spent one brief, romantic summer together before going their separate ways. Keira leaves her necklace behind in Adrian\'s apartment, sparking his interest as a scientist and fuelling his hopes for a rekindling of old passions. What innocently begins as a common pursuit of knowledge soon takes a dangerous turn when their guide is found dead. Despite heightening threats to their own safety, Keira and Adrian continue their search, which takes them across the world, from cutting edge laboratories to venerable museums, from forgotten Greek islands to monasteries hidden in the mountains. They follow maps written in the stars and clues buried within the earth, always guided by the slowly unraveling secrets of the strange object from Ethiopia.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/282080.Guillaume_Musso">About Guillaume Musso</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/282080.Guillaume_Musso"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1487686506p3/282080.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11052282697791016302">One of the most popular authors in France today. From his early childhood with reading books and plays, Guillaume Musso became convinced that one day, he too would write novels. After finishing high school in France, Guillaume Musso left for the United States at the age of 19. He spent several months in New York City, living with other young foreigners and earning his money by selling ice-cream. H</span>
  <span id="freeText11052282697791016302" style="display:none">One of the most popular authors in France today. From his early childhood with reading books and plays, Guillaume Musso became convinced that one day, he too would write novels. After finishing high school in France, Guillaume Musso left for the United States at the age of 19. He spent several months in New York City, living with other young foreigners and earning his money by selling ice-cream. He came home to France with his head filled with ideas for novels. The readers can easily see the influence his time in the United States has had on him, as the action in his books takes place overseas. He currently teaches in a high school in the south of France, all the while working on his novels. His first published novel was with Editions Anne Carriere in 2001: <i>Skidamarink</i>, this novel did not reach out to the masses however, but his following novels published on XO Editions have all been hugely successful, some of them translated into 20 languages. His novel, <i>Afterwards</i>, has been adapted to the big screen and was in cinemas January 2009, starring John Malkovich, Evangeline Lily and Romain Duris.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11052282697791016302" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
